8.86 Routine process controls should be implemented to ensure adherence to validated filtration parameters. Results of critical process parameters should be included in the batch record, including but not limited to the minimum time taken to filter a known volume of bulk solution and pressure difference across the filter. Any significant difference from critical parameters during manufacturing should be documented and investigated.

"8.87 The integrity of the sterilised filter assembly should be verified by integrity testing before use (pre-use post sterilisation integrity test or PUPSIT), to check for damage and loss of integrity caused by the filter preparation prior to use. A sterilising grade filter that is used to sterilise a fluid should be subject to a non-destructive integrity test post-use prior to removal of the filter from its housing..."

8.87 (continued) It is recognized that PUPSIT may not always be possible after sterilisation due to process constraints (e.g. the filtration of very small volumes of solution). In these cases, an alternative approach may be taken providing that a thorough risk assessment has been performed. Points to consider in such a risk assessment include:

  • i. in depth knowledge and control of the filter sterilisation process to minimize damage potential
  • ii. in depth knowledge of the supply chain (contract sterilisation facilities, transport, packaging)
  • iii. process knowledge: specific product type including particle burden; pre-filtration steps that remove particle burden

8.88 The integrity of critical sterile gas and air vent filters (directly linked to product sterility) should be verified by testing after use, with the filter remaining in the filter assembly or housing.

8.89 The integrity of non-critical air or gas vent filters should be confirmed and recorded at appropriate intervals. Where gas filters are in place for extended periods, integrity testing should be carried out at installation and prior to replacement. The maximum duration of use should be specified and monitored based on risk.

8.90 For gas filtration, unintended moistening or wetting of the filter or filter equipment should be avoided.

8.91 If the sterilising filtration process has been validated as a system consisting of multiple filters to achieve the sterility for a given fluid, the filtration system is considered to be a single sterilising unit and all filters within the system should satisfactorily pass integrity testing after use.

8.92 In a redundant filtration system (where a second redundant sterilising grade filter is present as a backup but the sterilising process is validated as only requiring one filter), post-use integrity test of the primary sterilising grade filter should be performed and if demonstrated to be integral, then a post-use integrity test of the redundant (backup) filter is not necessary. However, in the event of a failure of the post-use integrity test on the primary filter, post-use integrity test on the secondary (redundant) filter should be performed, in conjunction with an investigation and risk assessment.

8.93 Bioburden samples should be taken from the bulk product and immediately prior to the final sterile filtration. In case where a redundant filtration set-up is used, it should be taken prior to the first filter. Systems for taking samples should be designed so as not to introduce contamination.

8.94 Liquid sterilising grade filters should be discarded after the processing of a single batch and the same filter should not be used continuously for more than one working day unless such use has been validated.

8.95 Where campaign manufacture of a product has been appropriately justified in the CCS and validated, the filter user should: (i) assess and document risks for filter duration; (ii) conduct validation studies; (iii) document maximum validated duration; (iv) implement controls to remove contaminated or defective filters.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts — 除菌過濾系統

除菌過濾器（Sterilising Grade Filter）：孔徑最大 0.22 µm，經驗證可截留微生物，是無法終端滅菌（Terminal Sterilisation）產品的最後一道無菌保障。

微生物負荷前過濾器（Bioburden Reduction Prefilter）：置於除菌過濾器上游，用於降低液體中微生物負荷（Bioburden），減少最終除菌過濾器的負擔，延長濾器壽命並提高整體無菌保障。

系統設計原則（8.82）：除菌過濾系統必須最小化除菌後到灌裝前的無菌連接（Aseptic Connection）數量——每一個連接點都是潛在的污染風險。

吸附與浸出（Adsorption & Leaching）：濾器本身可能吸附藥物活性成分（影響濃度），或將濾器材料中的化學物質溶出至產品中——這兩者都必須評估。

比喻說明 Analogy — 除菌過濾的「最後安全門」

將除菌過濾系統想像成機場的安全通道：前段的行李 X 光機（bioburden reduction prefilter）先篩掉大件危險品；最後的人工安檢（0.22 µm 除菌濾器）才是正式的「放行確認」。Annex 1 要求這道最後安全門要盡可能靠近登機口（point of fill）——距離越短，安檢後被重新污染的風險越低。

★ 重大條款：PUPSIT（8.87）— 使用前滅菌後完整性測試

PUPSIT = Pre-Use Post-Sterilization Integrity Test（使用前滅菌後完整性測試）

濾器滅菌（通常是高壓蒸氣或 gamma 照射）後、使用前，必須先做一次完整性測試（integrity test），確認濾器在安裝與滅菌過程中未受損。過去許多廠商只做使用後測試（post-use），2022 年版 Annex 1 明確要求使用前也需測試。

測試方法：起泡點法（Bubble Point）、擴散流法（Diffusive Flow）、水浸入法（Water Intrusion）、壓力保持法（Pressure Hold Test）

豁免條件：僅在有充分科學依據且完成徹底風險評估後方可豁免（例如極小體積過濾），且必須有補償性控制措施。

比喻說明 — PUPSIT：出門前檢查瓦斯

PUPSIT 就像出門前檢查瓦斯爐是否關好：瓦斯爐（濾器）可能在安裝時就已損壞，如果不事先檢查，等到你回家（使用後才測試）發現問題，整批藥品可能已無菌保障全失。

以前的做法是：用完才測試（post-use only）——萬一那批藥品過濾時濾器就已破損，整批放行都是無效的無菌保障。PUPSIT 就是要在「使用前」就確認濾器完好。

重點提示 — 使用後完整性測試（Post-Use）同樣必要

8.87 也要求除菌濾器在過濾完成後、拆除前，必須做使用後完整性測試（Post-Use Integrity Test）。這是確認「過濾過程中濾器是否完整」的最終確認。兩個測試缺一不可：

  • Pre-use（PUPSIT）：確認濾器在滅菌與安裝時未損壞
  • Post-use：確認過濾過程中濾器始終完整

核心概念 — 冗餘過濾系統（8.92）

冗餘過濾系統（Redundant Filtration System）：安裝兩個串聯的除菌濾器，但驗證僅需一個即可達到無菌保障。第二個（備用）濾器是安全保障。

實務邏輯：若主過濾器（primary）通過使用後完整性測試，備用過濾器（redundant）不需測試。若主過濾器測試失敗，則對備用過濾器進行測試，同時啟動調查。這代表只要備用濾器完整，批次放行仍有可能。

重點提示 — 微生物負荷採樣時機（8.93）

微生物負荷（Bioburden）採樣必須在最終除菌過濾「緊接之前（immediately prior to）」執行。若為冗餘系統，則在第一個濾器前採樣。

目的：確認進入除菌濾器的液體微生物負荷在可接受範圍內，作為無菌保障的輸入控制（input control）。高微生物負荷可能堵塞或損壞濾器，增加過濾失敗風險。

重點提示 — 濾器一次性使用原則（8.94）

除菌液體濾器原則上僅供單批次使用，且同一濾器不得連續使用超過一個工作天，除非經過驗證。

例外情況（8.95）：連續生產（Campaign Manufacture）場景下，可在充分評估、記錄風險並完成驗證後，使用更長時間。但必須明確規定最大驗證使用期限，並嚴格管控。

實務應用 Practical Application — CDMO 的 PUPSIT 實施挑戰

在 CDMO 環境中，PUPSIT 帶來實際挑戰：

  • 設備設計：過濾系統必須設計成允許在滅菌後、充填前進行完整性測試的能力（通常需要增加壓力感測器和閥門）
  • SOP 更新：2022 年版 Annex 1 發布後，現有 SOP 必須更新，並對操作人員重新培訓
  • 豁免申請：小批量客戶產品若無法進行 PUPSIT，需要正式的書面風險評估，並在 CCS 中記錄補償性控制措施

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. PUPSIT 與傳統的「使用後完整性測試（post-use integrity test）」有何本質差異？為何 Annex 1 (2022) 認為只做使用後測試是不夠的？
  2. 一家製造商表示他們的產品體積極小（5 mL），難以執行 PUPSIT。他們應如何處理此情況？需要哪些文件？
  3. 在冗餘過濾系統中，若主濾器失敗了使用後完整性測試，批次是否必然被拒絕？說明決策流程。
8.96–8.104 Form-Fill-Seal (FFS) — 成型充填密封

原文內容 Original Text

8.96 The conditions for FFS machines used for terminally sterilised products should comply with the environmental requirements of paragraphs 8.3 and 8.4 of this Annex. The conditions for FFS machines used in aseptic manufacture should comply with the environmental requirements of paragraph 8.10 of this Annex.

8.97 Contamination of the packaging films used in the FFS process should be minimized by appropriate controls during component fabrication, supply and handling. Due to the criticality of packaging films, procedures should be implemented to ensure that the films supplied meet defined specifications and are of the appropriate quality, including material thickness and strength, microbial and particulate contamination, integrity and artwork, as relevant. The sampling frequency, the bioburden and, where applicable, endotoxin/pyrogen levels of packaging films and associated components should be defined and controlled within the PQS and considered in the CCS.

8.98 Particular attention should be given to understanding and assessing the operation of the equipment, including set-up, filling, sealing and cutting processes, so that critical process parameters are understood, validated, controlled and monitored appropriately.

8.99 Any product contact gases, e.g. those used to inflate the container or used as a product overlay, should be appropriately filtered, as close to the point of use as possible. The quality of gases used and the effectiveness of gas filtration systems should be verified periodically in accordance with paragraphs 6.18 and 6.19.

8.100 The controls identified during qualification of FFS should be in alignment with the CCS. Aspects to be considered include but are not limited to:

  • i. determination of the boundaries of the critical zone
  • ii. environmental control and monitoring, both of the machine and the background
  • iii. personnel gowning requirements
  • iv. integrity testing of the product filling lines and filtration systems (as relevant)
  • v. duration of the batch or filling campaign
  • vi. control of packaging films, including any requirements for film decontamination or sterilisation
  • vii. cleaning-in-place and sterilisation-in-place of equipment as necessary
  • viii. machine operation, settings and alarm management (as relevant)

8.101 Critical process parameters for FFS should be determined during equipment qualification and should include, but are not limited to:

  • i. settings for uniform package dimensions and cutting in accordance with validated parameters
  • ii. setting, maintenance and monitoring of validated forming temperatures (including pre-heating and cooling), forming times and pressures
  • iii. setting, maintenance and monitoring of validated sealing temperatures, sealing temperature uniformity across the seal, sealing times and pressures
  • iv. environmental and product temperature
  • v. batch-specific testing of package seal strength and uniformity
  • vi. settings for correct filling volumes, speeds and uniformity
  • vii. settings for any additional printing (batch coding), embossing or debossing to ensure unit integrity is not compromised
  • viii. methods and parameters for integrity testing of filled containers (see paragraph 8.22)

8.102 Appropriate procedures for the verification, monitoring and recording of FFS critical process parameters and equipment operation should be applied during production.

8.103 Operational procedures should describe how forming and sealing issues are detected and rectified. Rejected units or sealing issues should be recorded and investigated.

8.104 Appropriate maintenance procedures should be established based on risk, and include maintenance and inspection plans for tooling critical to the effectiveness of unit sealing. Any issues identified that indicate a potential product quality concern should be documented and investigated.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts — FFS 技術

成型充填密封（Form-Fill-Seal, FFS）：一種整合式包裝技術，使用卷膜（web film）在同一機台上完成容器成型（forming）、藥液充填（filling）、密封（sealing）和切割（cutting）。常見於輸液軟袋、眼藥水等。

終端滅菌 vs 無菌充填的分級差異：

  • 終端滅菌（Terminally Sterilised）產品的 FFS：遵循 8.3/8.4 條款（背景區域要求）
  • 無菌充填（Aseptic Manufacture）的 FFS：遵循 8.10 條款（Grade A 充填區）

這是 FFS 在法規上最關鍵的區分點——同樣的設備，使用場景不同，環境要求截然不同。

比喻說明 Analogy — FFS 像生產線上的「自動包裝機」

FFS 就像便利商店的三明治自動包裝機：原料（薄膜）從一端進入，在同一台機器上自動完成成型、填料、密封。藥廠的 FFS 機台的核心挑戰是：密封品質（sealing quality）取決於溫度、壓力、時間的精確控制——任何一個參數偏差都可能導致密封不完全，直接危害藥品無菌性和穩定性。

重點提示 — 包裝薄膜的生物負荷控制（8.97）

FFS 的包裝薄膜（packaging film）是無菌保障鏈中的關鍵輸入材料。Annex 1 要求：

  • 薄膜的 Bioburden（微生物負荷）和 endotoxin/pyrogen 水平必須被定義和管控
  • 這些控制要納入 PQS（產品品質系統）和 CCS（污染控制策略）
  • 薄膜的厚度、強度、完整性、artwork 都必須符合規格

這意味著薄膜供應商管理是 FFS 無菌保障的重要環節，不能只管製程本身。

FFS 關鍵製程參數（CPP）摘要

FFS CPP 矩陣（8.101）：
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
成型參數：
  - 成型溫度（預熱/冷卻）
  - 成型時間與壓力
  - 包裝尺寸均一性

密封參數（最關鍵）：
  - 密封溫度（上下均一性）
  - 密封時間與壓力
  - 密封強度測試（每批次）

充填參數：
  - 充填體積、速度、均一性
  - 批號印刷/壓印設定

品質確認：
  - 100% 密封完整性測試（8.22）
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

實務應用 — CDMO 接受 FFS 新客戶的評估重點

當 CDMO 評估一個新的 FFS 客戶專案時，需優先確認：

  • 終端滅菌 or 無菌充填？ 決定了環境監控等級和 CCS 複雜度
  • 包裝薄膜規格：客戶提供的薄膜是否有符合 Annex 1 要求的 Bioburden/endotoxin COA？
  • 密封驗證：目前 FFS 機台的密封溫度/壓力驗證報告（PQ）是否涵蓋客戶的薄膜規格？
  • CCS 整合：客戶的包裝薄膜管控是否已整合進廠內的 CCS 文件？

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. FFS 用於終端滅菌產品與無菌充填產品，在環境分級上有何不同？為什麼？
  2. 一個 FFS 批次發現有部分容器密封強度低於規格。依 8.103/8.104，應如何處理？需要哪些文件？
  3. 為何 FFS 的包裝薄膜需要控制 endotoxin/pyrogen 水平（8.97）？這與產品品質有何關聯？
8.105–8.120 Blow-Fill-Seal (BFS) — 吹塑充填密封

原文內容 Original Text

8.105 Blow-Fill-Seal equipment used for terminally sterilised products should be installed in at least a grade D environment. The conditions at the point of fill should comply with the environmental requirements of paragraphs 8.3 and 8.4.

8.106 BFS used for aseptic processing:

  • i. For shuttle type equipment used for aseptic filling, the parison is open to the environment and therefore the areas where parison extrusion, blow-moulding and sealing take place should meet grade A conditions at the critical zones. The filling environment should be designed and maintained to meet grade A conditions for viable and total particle limits both at rest and when in operation.
  • ii. For rotary-type equipment used for aseptic filling, the parison is generally closed to the environment once formed, the filling environment within the parison should be designed and maintained to meet grade A conditions for viable and total particle limits both at rest and when in operation.
  • iii. The equipment should be installed in at least a grade C environment, provided that grade A/B clothing is used. The microbiological monitoring of operators wearing grade A/B clothing in a grade C area should be performed in accordance with risk management principles.

8.107 Due to the generation of particles from polymer extrusion and cutting during operation, and the restrictive size of critical filling zones of BFS equipment, in operation monitoring of total particle for BFS equipment is not expected. However, data should be available to demonstrate that the design of the equipment ensures that critical zones of the filling process environment would meet grade A conditions in operation.

8.108 Viable environmental monitoring of BFS processes should be risk-based, and designed in accordance with section 9 of this Annex. In operation viable monitoring should be undertaken for the full duration of critical processing, including equipment assembly. For rotary-type BFS equipment, it is acknowledged that monitoring of the critical filling zone may not be possible.

8.109 The environmental control and monitoring programme should take into consideration the moving parts and complex airflow paths generated by the BFS process and the effect of the high heat outputs of the process (e.g. through the use of airflow visualization studies and/or other equivalent studies). Environmental monitoring programmes should also consider factors such as air-filter configuration, air-filter integrity, cooling systems integrity, equipment design and qualification.

8.110 Air or other gases that make contact with critical surfaces of the container during extrusion, formation or sealing of the moulded container should undergo appropriate filtration. The quality of gas used and the effectiveness of gas filtration systems should be verified periodically.

8.111 Particulate and microbial contamination of the polymer granulate should be prevented by appropriate design, control, and maintenance of the polymer granulate storage, sampling and distribution systems.

8.112 The capability of the extrusion system to provide appropriate sterility assurance for the moulded container should be understood and validated. The sampling frequency, the bioburden and, where applicable, endotoxin/pyrogen levels of the raw polymer should be defined and controlled within the PQS and considered in the CCS.

8.113 Interventions requiring cessation of filling and/or extrusion, moulding and sealing and, where required, re-sterilisation of the filling machine should be clearly defined and described in the filling procedure, and included in the APS.

8.114 The controls identified during qualification of BFS should be in alignment with the site's CCS. Aspects to be considered include but are not limited to:

  • i. determination of the boundaries of the critical zone
  • ii. environmental control and monitoring, both of the machine and the background
  • iii. personnel gowning requirements
  • iv. integrity testing of the product filling lines and filtration systems (as relevant)
  • v. duration of the batch or filling campaign
  • vi. control of polymer granulate, including distribution systems and critical extrusion temperatures
  • vii. cleaning-in-place and sterilisation-in-place of equipment as necessary
  • viii. machine operation, settings and alarm management (as relevant)

8.115 Critical process parameters for BFS should be determined during equipment qualification and should include, but are not limited to:

  • i. CIP and SIP of product pipelines and filling needles (mandrels)
  • ii. extrusion parameters: temperature, speed, extruder throat settings for parison thickness
  • iii. mould temperatures, including rate of cooling for product stability
  • iv. preparation and sterilisation of ancillary components (e.g. bottle caps)
  • v. environmental control, cleaning, sterilisation and monitoring of critical extrusion, transfer and filling areas
  • vi. batch-specific testing of package wall-thickness at critical points
  • vii. settings for correct filling volumes, speeds and uniformity
  • viii. settings for printing (batch coding), embossing or debossing
  • ix. methods and parameters for integrity testing of 100% of all filled containers (see paragraph 8.22)
  • x. settings for cutters or punches used to remove waste plastic surrounding filled units (flash removal)

8.116 Appropriate procedures for the verification, monitoring and recording of BFS critical process parameters and equipment operation should be applied during production.

8.117 Operational procedures should describe how blowing, forming and sealing issues are detected and rectified. Rejected units or sealing issues should be recorded and investigated.

8.118 Where the BFS process includes the addition of components to moulded containers (e.g. addition of caps to LVP bottles), these components should be appropriately decontaminated:

  • i. For aseptic processes: addition of components should be performed under grade A conditions, using pre-sterilised components
  • ii. For terminally sterilised products: validation of terminal sterilisation should ensure sterility of all critical product pathways, including areas not wetted during sterilisation
  • iii. Testing procedures should be established and validated to ensure effective sealing of components and moulded containers

8.119 Appropriate maintenance procedures should be established based on risk, and include maintenance and inspection plans for items critical to unit sealing, integrity and sterility.

8.120 The moulds used to form containers are considered critical equipment and any changes or modification to moulds should result in an assessment of finished product container integrity, and where the assessment indicates, should be supported by validation.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts — BFS 技術特性

吹塑充填密封（Blow-Fill-Seal, BFS）：從聚合物顆粒（polymer granulate）出發，在同一機台上完成：擠出（extrusion）→ 吹塑成型（blow-moulding）→ 充填（filling）→ 密封（sealing）。整個過程不依賴預製容器，是高度整合的無菌充填技術。

兩種主要機型：

  • 往復式（Shuttle Type）：型胚（parison）在成型時對外部環境開放，關鍵區域需達 Grade A
  • 旋轉式（Rotary Type）：型胚成型後通常在封閉環境中，但旋轉結構使關鍵充填區的環境監控較為困難

比喻說明 Analogy — BFS 像「現場鑄瓶立刻裝藥」

BFS 就像一家礦泉水工廠：塑膠顆粒進來，機器先把它熔化、吹成瓶子（blow-moulding），瓶口還沒完全冷卻就立刻注入水，然後立刻密封。整個過程在幾秒內完成，容器從未暴露在外部環境中。

這就是 BFS 無菌保障的核心優勢：容器「出生」的瞬間就被充填和密封，幾乎沒有機會被污染。但代價是：高溫擠出和切割過程產生大量微粒，使得「在線粒子監控」（in operation total particle monitoring）幾乎不可能——Annex 1 在 8.107 明確認可了這一點。

重點提示 — BFS 的粒子監控豁免（8.107）

8.107 是 Annex 1 中少見的「承認監控限制」條款：由於 BFS 製程本身會產生大量聚合物擠出和切割微粒，加上充填關鍵區空間狹小，不要求進行充填過程中的總粒子數監控（in-operation total particle monitoring）。

但這不代表完全免除責任——廠商必須有設計驗證數據（design qualification data），証明設備設計確保關鍵充填區在運作時能達到 Grade A 條件。

重點提示 — 聚合物顆粒的無菌保障（8.112）

BFS 的無菌保障不只在製程端——原料端的聚合物顆粒（polymer granulate）同樣需要被管控。Annex 1 要求：

  • 擠出系統對成型容器提供無菌保障的能力必須被理解和驗證
  • 原始聚合物的微生物負荷（bioburden）和內毒素（endotoxin/pyrogen）水平必須被定義和管控
  • 這些控制要整合進 PQS 和 CCS

高溫擠出過程本身提供了一定的熱殺菌效果，但這必須被明確驗證，而不能僅憑假設。

BFS 環境要求對比表

終端滅菌產品的 BFS（8.105）：
  背景環境：最低 Grade D
  充填點：符合 8.3/8.4 要求

無菌充填的 BFS（8.106）：
  往復式設備（Shuttle Type）：
    關鍵區（擠出/吹塑/密封）：Grade A
    背景環境：最低 Grade C（著 A/B 潔淨服）
  旋轉式設備（Rotary Type）：
    型胚內充填環境：Grade A
    背景環境：最低 Grade C（著 A/B 潔淨服）

在線粒子監控（8.107）：
  不要求 in-operation 總粒子監控
  但需設計驗證數據支持 Grade A 達成

核心概念 — 模具是關鍵設備（8.120）

BFS 的模具（moulds）被明確定義為關鍵設備（critical equipment）。任何對模具的變更或修改，都必須：

  • 對成品容器完整性進行重新評估
  • 若評估結果顯示有影響，必須進行驗證

這是因為模具直接決定容器壁厚、容量和密封品質，模具的任何磨損或修改都可能改變這些關鍵參數，進而影響容器的密封完整性（CCI）和無菌性。

實務應用 — BFS 在 CDMO 的客戶論證

CDMO 向新客戶展示 BFS 技術的無菌保障時，需要能夠解釋：

  • 設計驗證（DQ）如何証明充填關鍵區達到 Grade A（即使無法做在線監控）
  • 聚合物顆粒供應商如何管控 bioburden，以及廠內如何驗證儲存和分配系統
  • 模具變更管理流程（Change Control），包括何時觸發容器完整性重新驗證
  • 在線 100% 容器完整性測試（CCI）方法及其與 8.22 的合規性

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為何 BFS 設備的往復式（shuttle type）和旋轉式（rotary type）在無菌充填場景下的環境要求不同？解釋背後的技術原因。
  2. 8.107 說 BFS 在運作時「不要求（not expected）」總粒子監控。這是否意味著廠商對充填區環境品質完全沒有責任？
  3. BFS 加蓋（caps）操作（8.118）在無菌充填和終端滅菌場景下有何不同要求？為什麼？
8.121–8.126 Lyophilization — 冷凍乾燥

原文內容 Original Text

8.121 Lyophilization is a critical process step and all activities that can affect the sterility of the product or material need to be regarded as extensions of the aseptic processing of the sterilised product. The lyophilization equipment and its processes should be designed to ensure that product or material sterility is maintained during lyophilization by preventing microbial and particle contamination between the filling of products for lyophilization, and completion of lyophilization process. All control measures in place should be determined by the site's CCS.

8.122 The sterilisation of the lyophilizer and associated equipment (e.g. trays, vial support rings) should be validated and the holding time between the sterilisation cycle and use appropriately challenged during APS (see paragraph 9.33). The lyophilizer should be sterilised regularly, based on system design. Re-sterilisation should be performed following maintenance or cleaning. Sterilised lyophilizers and associated equipment should be protected from contamination after sterilisation.

"8.123 Lyophilizers and associated product transfer and loading/unloading areas should be designed to minimize operator intervention as far as possible. The frequency of lyophilizer sterilisation should be determined based on the design and risks related to system contamination during use. Lyophilizers that are manually loaded or unloaded with no barrier technology separation should be sterilised before each load. For lyophilizers loaded and unloaded by automated systems or protected by closed barrier systems, the frequency of sterilisation should be justified and documented as part of the CCS."

8.124 The integrity of the lyophilizer should be maintained following sterilisation and during lyophilization. The filter used to maintain lyophilizer integrity should be sterilised before each use of the system and its integrity testing results should be part of the batch certification/release. The frequency of vacuum/leak integrity testing of the chamber should be documented and the maximum permitted leakage of air into the lyophilizer should be specified and checked at the start of every cycle.

8.125 Lyophilization trays should be checked regularly to ensure that they are not misshapen or damaged.

8.126 Points to consider for the design of loading (and unloading, where the lyophilized material is still unsealed and exposed), include but are not limited to:

  • i. The loading pattern within the lyophilizer should be specified and documented
  • ii. The transfer of partially closed containers to a lyophilizer should be undertaken under grade A conditions at all times and handled in a manner designed to minimize direct operator intervention. Technologies such as conveyor systems or portable transfer systems (e.g. clean air transfer carts, portable unidirectional airflow workstations) should be used. Alternatively, trays closed in grade A and not reopened whilst in the grade B area may be used to protect partially stoppered vials (e.g. appropriately closed boxes).
  • iii. Airflow patterns should not be adversely affected by transport devices and venting of the loading zone
  • iv. Unsealed containers (such as partially stoppered vials) should be maintained under grade A conditions and should normally be separated from operators by physical barrier technology or any other appropriate measures
  • v. Where seating of the stoppers is not completed prior to opening the lyophilizer chamber, product removed from the lyophilizer should remain under grade A conditions during subsequent handling
  • vi. Utensils used during loading and unloading of the lyophilizer (e.g. trays, bags, placing devices, tweezers) should be sterile

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts — 冷凍乾燥的無菌延伸性

冷凍乾燥（Lyophilization）：在低溫真空環境下，將藥品中的水分從固態冰直接昇華為水蒸氣，以去除水分並延長藥品穩定性。冷凍乾燥機（Lyophilizer）是整個無菌製程的延伸——充填完成的半加蓋瓶（partially stoppered vials）仍處於「未封口」狀態，直到冷凍乾燥完成後才真正完成密封。

8.121 明確定義：冷凍乾燥是無菌製程的延伸（extension of aseptic processing）。這代表所有裝載、轉移、卸載操作都必須維持與無菌充填相同等級的污染控制。

比喻說明 Analogy — 冷凍乾燥機是「無菌製程的延伸手術室」

冷凍乾燥機就像手術室的一個「後備室」：手術（充填）完成後，病人（半加蓋瓶）還需要在另一個無菌空間（冷凍乾燥機）繼續接受治療（乾燥），期間傷口（瓶口）仍然暴露，無菌環境的要求一刻都不能鬆懈。

這就是為什麼冷凍乾燥機本身需要定期滅菌，且從充填站到冷凍乾燥機的轉移路徑必須全程維持 Grade A 條件。

延後實施通知 — 8.123 條款（重要！）

8.123 條款中關於「手動裝載無屏障冷凍乾燥機須在每次裝載前進行滅菌」的要求，已推遲至 2024 年 8 月 25 日實施。

原始 Annex 1 (2022) 要求：手動裝載/卸載且無屏障技術分隔的冷凍乾燥機，須在每次裝載前滅菌。對於許多尚未自動化的廠房，這是一個重大的操作負擔，PIC/S 給予了緩衝期。

實務含義：廠商應檢視目前的冷凍乾燥機裝載方式，評估是否符合此要求，並將滅菌頻率決策明確記錄於 CCS 中。如果仍是手動裝載無屏障，應在 2024 年 8 月 25 日前完成合規改善或文件更新。

重點提示 — 冷凍乾燥機完整性測試（8.124）

冷凍乾燥機的完整性（integrity）管控包含兩個層面：

  • 濾器完整性：用於維持冷凍乾燥機完整性的過濾器必須在每次使用前滅菌，且其完整性測試結果必須作為批次放行（batch certification/release）的一部分
  • 腔體真空/洩漏完整性：腔體的真空/洩漏完整性測試頻率必須文件化，且每個循環開始前必須確認最大允許洩漏量（maximum permitted leakage）

這意味著冷凍乾燥機的完整性測試結果是批次放行的必要文件，不是選擇性監控。

重點提示 — 裝載設計與半加蓋瓶保護（8.126）

8.126 列出了冷凍乾燥機裝載設計的關鍵考量點，核心原則是：

  • 半加蓋瓶從充填站到冷凍乾燥機的轉移必須全程在 Grade A 下進行
  • 未封口容器必須與操作人員進行物理屏障隔離
  • 所有接觸冷凍乾燥機的器具（托盤、夾具、鑷子等）必須是無菌的
  • 冷凍乾燥機腔體開門後，若塞子尚未完全壓入，產品必須繼續在 Grade A 下處理

冷凍乾燥機滅菌頻率決策樹

問題：冷凍乾燥機如何裝載/卸載？
        │
        ├── 手動裝載，無屏障技術隔離
        │     → 每次裝載前滅菌（8.123）
        │       [注意：此要求延後至 2024/08/25 實施]
        │
        └── 自動化系統 OR 封閉屏障系統保護
              → 滅菌頻率可調整
                但必須：
                - 有科學依據
                - 記錄於 CCS
                - 定期審查

另外，以下情況必須重新滅菌（8.122）：
  - 維護（Maintenance）後
  - 清潔（Cleaning）後

實務應用 — 冷凍乾燥機升級投資評估

8.123 的要求促使許多 CDMO 重新評估手動冷凍乾燥機的改造投資：

  • 現狀評估：手動裝載無屏障系統 → 每批前滅菌 → 增加生產時間和蒸汽消耗
  • 升級選項：安裝自動裝載系統（automated loading system）或 RABS/Isolator 屏障 → 可降低滅菌頻率，提高生產效率
  • ROI 計算：節省的滅菌時間 × 批次數量 × 設備利用率 vs 升級資本支出
  • CCS 更新：無論升級與否，滅菌頻率的決策依據必須明確記錄於 CCS

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 為何冷凍乾燥過程被定義為「無菌製程的延伸（extension of aseptic processing）」而不是獨立製程步驟？這對環境要求有何影響？
  2. 一家工廠的冷凍乾燥機目前是手動裝載，沒有屏障技術。根據 8.123，他們目前的操作是否合規？他們有哪些選項？
  3. 冷凍乾燥機的完整性測試結果（8.124）必須作為批次放行文件的一部分。請說明這在批次記錄（Batch Record）中應如何被記錄。
8.127–8.130 Closed Systems — 密閉系統

原文內容 Original Text

8.127 The use of closed systems can reduce the risk of microbial, particle and chemical contamination from the adjacent environment. Closed systems should always be designed to reduce the need for manual manipulations and the associated risks.

8.128 It is critical to ensure the sterility of all product contact surfaces of closed systems used for aseptic processing. The design and selection of any closed system used for aseptic processing should ensure maintenance of sterility. Connection of sterile equipment (e.g. tubing/pipework) to the sterilised product pathway after the final sterilising grade filter should be designed to be connected aseptically (e.g. by intrinsic sterile connection devices).

8.129 Appropriate measures should be in place to ensure the integrity of components used in aseptic connections. The means by which this is achieved should be determined and captured in the CCS. Appropriate system integrity tests should be considered when there is a risk of compromising product sterility. Supplier assessment should include the collation of data in relation to potential failure modes that may lead to a loss of system sterility.

8.130 The background environment in which closed systems are located should be based on their design and the processes undertaken. For aseptic processing and where there are any risks that system integrity may be compromised, the system should be located in grade A. If the system can be shown to remain integral at every usage (e.g. via pressure testing and/or monitoring) then a lower classified area may be used. Any transfer between classified areas should be thoroughly assessed (see paragraph 4.10).

If the closed system is opened (e.g. for maintenance of a bulk manufacturing line) then this should be performed in a classified area appropriate to the materials (e.g. grade C for terminal sterilisation processes, or grade A for aseptic processing) or be subject to further cleaning and disinfection (and sterilisation in case of aseptic processes).

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts — 密閉系統定義

密閉系統（Closed System）：在無菌製程中，指一個與外部環境完全隔離的液體處理系統，產品不暴露於周圍環境。典型例子：無菌轉移管路、一次性使用袋（Single-Use Bag）系統、整合式過濾充填管路。

密閉系統的三大保護優勢：

  • 降低微生物污染（microbial contamination）風險
  • 降低微粒污染（particle contamination）風險
  • 降低化學污染（chemical contamination）風險

設計核心原則：最小化手動操作（minimize manual manipulations）。每次人工介入都是污染風險的增加點。

比喻說明 Analogy — 密閉系統像「封閉式輸血管路」

密閉系統就像醫院的靜脈輸液管路：從血袋到患者手臂的整條路徑都是封閉的，血液（藥液）在整個轉移過程中不暴露於空氣。如果需要在中途接上另一條管路（aseptic connection），必須使用特殊的無菌連接裝置（sterile connector），而不能打開系統暴露在空氣中。

8.128 的核心要求就是：除菌濾器後的管路連接，必須使用能保持系統無菌的連接方式（例如 sterile weld 或 aseptic connector），不能用普通的螺紋接頭或手動打開連接。

重點提示 — 無菌連接設備（8.128/8.129）

在除菌濾器後的所有管路連接必須設計為「本質上無菌（intrinsically sterile）」的連接方式。常見的合規解決方案：

  • 無菌焊接（Sterile Weld / Tube Welding）：使用熱融焊接技術在封閉環境中連接管路，連接點本身就是無菌的
  • 無菌快速連接器（Aseptic Connector）：設計為可在非無菌環境下連接但保持連接點無菌的專用接頭
  • Rapid Transfer Port (RTP)：快速傳遞口，用於密閉系統之間的無菌轉移

供應商評估（supplier assessment）必須包含潛在失效模式（failure modes）的數據收集，這是 CCS 的必要輸入。

密閉系統背景環境決策矩陣（8.130）

問題：密閉系統應放置在何種環境分級？
        │
        ├── 無菌製程 AND 有任何系統完整性被破壞的風險
        │     → Grade A
        │
        ├── 無菌製程 AND 可通過壓力測試/監控
        │   證明系統在每次使用時均保持完整
        │     → 可使用較低分級區域
        │       （但需評估並文件化）
        │
        └── 密閉系統被開啟（如：維護）：
              - 終端滅菌製程 → Grade C
              - 無菌製程     → Grade A
              OR
              進行清潔、消毒（無菌製程需加上滅菌）

實務應用 — 密閉系統評估在 CDMO 的商業意義

密閉系統設計的好壞直接影響 CDMO 的競爭力：

  • 背景環境降級的可能性：如果能夠充分論證密閉系統的完整性（8.130），可能將操作從 Grade A 降至較低分級，顯著降低環境監控成本和複雜度
  • 供應商選擇：無菌連接器、焊接設備的選擇直接影響系統完整性——需要供應商提供失效模式數據（failure mode data）作為 CCS 的輸入
  • 一次性使用系統（SUS）整合：SUS 本質上是密閉系統的延伸，8.127-8.130 的要求對 SUS 的設計選型有直接指導意義（參見 8.131-8.139）

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 密閉系統（8.127）如何改變傳統無菌製程的污染控制策略？它能否完全取代嚴格的環境分級要求？
  2. 根據 8.130，一個密閉系統的背景環境在什麼條件下可以從 Grade A 降級到較低分級？需要哪些文件支持？
  3. 若在無菌製程中需要開啟密閉系統進行維護，應在何種環境分級下進行？事後需要做什麼？

本節重點回顧 Section 8C Summary

  • 除菌過濾（8.79-8.95）：PUPSIT（使用前滅菌後完整性測試）是 Annex 1 (2022) 的強制要求，豁免須有充分風險評估和補償控制；微生物負荷採樣必須在最終過濾前緊接執行；除菌濾器原則上單批次使用
  • FFS（8.96-8.104）：終端滅菌與無菌充填適用不同環境分級；包裝薄膜的 Bioburden/endotoxin 控制必須納入 PQS 和 CCS；密封溫度均一性是最關鍵的 CPP
  • BFS（8.105-8.120）：高溫擠出製程免除在線總粒子監控要求，但需設計驗證數據；原始聚合物的微生物負荷也需管控；模具是關鍵設備，任何修改需重新評估容器完整性
  • 冷凍乾燥（8.121-8.126）：冷凍乾燥是無菌製程的延伸，全程需維持無菌條件；8.123 手動裝載每批前滅菌要求已延後至 2024 年 8 月 25 日實施；冷凍乾燥機完整性測試結果是批次放行必要文件
  • 密閉系統（8.127-8.130）：除菌濾器後的管路連接必須使用本質上無菌的連接方式（如無菌焊接、無菌連接器）；密閉系統可在論證完整性後使用較低分級背景環境

決策層次提醒 Decision Hierarchy

1. 無菌保證 Sterility Assurance — 永遠第一
▼
2. 產品關鍵品質屬性 CQAs — 患者安全
▼
3. 商業與操作彈性 Business Flexibility — 最後考量

本節所有技術選擇（PUPSIT、環境分級、滅菌頻率、密閉系統設計）都必須以無菌保證為最高優先。

9

Section 9: Environmental and Process Monitoring

環境與製程監測 | p41-p50

PIC/S Annex 1 (2022) — Manufacture of Sterile Medicinal Products | p41 – p50
PIC/S

本章學習目標

  • 理解環境監測計畫（Environmental Monitoring Programme）的設計原則，包括風險評估驅動的採樣位置、頻率與方法選擇。
  • 區分警戒限（Alert Level）與行動限（Action Limit）的定義、設定依據及超限後的因應程序。
  • 熟悉活性微生物監測（Viable Particle Monitoring）與非活性粒子監測（Non-viable Particle Monitoring）的方法及各等級要求，並能正確解讀 Table 5 與 Table 6 的法規限值。
  • 深入了解無菌製程模擬（Aseptic Process Simulation, APS）又稱培養基灌充（Media Fill）的設計、執行頻率、合格標準、失敗調查與批次處置要求。
  • 掌握 APS 在 RABS、隔離器（Isolator）及凍乾製程中的特殊考量，以及操作人員資格維護的要求。
9.4–9.13 環境監測計畫設計、警戒限與行動限

原文內容 Original Text

9.4 An environmental monitoring programme should be established and documented. The purpose of the environmental monitoring programme, is to:

  1. Provide assurance that cleanrooms and clean air equipment continue to provide an environment of appropriate air cleanliness, in accordance with design and regulatory requirements.
  2. Effectively detect excursions from environmental limits triggering investigation and assessment of risk to product quality.

Risk assessments should be performed in order to establish this comprehensive environmental monitoring programme, i.e. sampling locations, frequency of monitoring, monitoring methods and incubation conditions (e.g. time, temperature(s), aerobic and/or anaerobic conditions).

These risk assessments should be conducted based on detailed knowledge of; the process inputs and final product, the facility, equipment, the criticality of specific processes and steps, the operations involved, routine monitoring data, monitoring data obtained during qualification and knowledge of typical microbial flora isolated from the environment.

The risk assessment should include the determination of critical monitoring locations, those locations where the presence of microorganisms during processing may have an impact upon product quality, (e.g. grade A, aseptic processing areas and the grade B areas that directly interface with the grade A area). Consideration of other information such as air visualisation studies should also be included. These risk assessments should be reviewed regularly in order to confirm the effectiveness of the site's environmental monitoring programme. The monitoring programme should be considered in the overall context of the trend analysis and the CCS for the site.

9.5 Routine monitoring of cleanrooms, clean air equipment and personnel should be performed in operation throughout all critical stages of processing, including equipment set-up.

9.6 Other characteristics, such as temperature and relative humidity, should be controlled within ranges that align with product/processing/personnel requirements and support maintenance of defined cleanliness standards (e.g. grade A or B).

9.7 The monitoring of grade A should demonstrate the maintenance of aseptic processing conditions during critical operations. Monitoring should be performed at locations posing the highest risk of contamination to the sterile equipment surfaces, containers, closures and product. The selection of monitoring locations and the orientation and positioning of sampling devices should be justified and appropriate to obtain reliable data from the critical zones.

9.8 Sampling methods should not pose a risk of contamination to the manufacturing operations.

9.9 Appropriate alert levels and action limits should be set for the results of viable and total particle monitoring. The maximum total particle action limits are described in Table 5 and the maximum viable particle action limits are described in Table 6. However, more stringent action limits may be applied based on data trending, the nature of the process or as determined within the CCS. Both viable and total particle alert levels should be established based on results of cleanroom qualification tests and periodically reviewed based on ongoing trend data.

9.10 Alert levels for grade A (total particle only) grade B, grade C and grade D should be set such that adverse trends (e.g. a numbers of events or individual events that indicate a deterioration of environmental control) are detected and addressed.

9.11 Monitoring procedures should define the approach to trending. Trends should include, but are not limited to:

  1. increasing numbers of excursions from action limits or alert levels;
  2. consecutive excursions from alert levels;
  3. regular but isolated excursion from action limits that may have a common cause, (e.g. single excursions that always follow planned preventative maintenance);
  4. changes in microbial flora type and numbers and predominance of specific organisms. Particular attention should be given to organisms recovered that may indicate a loss of control, deterioration in cleanliness or organisms that may be difficult to control such as spore-forming microorganisms and moulds.

9.12 The monitoring of grade C and D cleanrooms in operation should be performed based on data collected during qualification and routine data to allow effective trend analysis. The requirements of alert levels and action limits will depend on the nature of the operations carried out. Action limits may be more stringent than those listed in Table 5 and Table 6.

9.13 If action limits are exceeded, operating procedures should prescribe a root cause investigation, an assessment of the potential impact to product (including batches produced between the monitoring and reporting) and requirements for corrective and preventive actions. If alert levels are exceeded, operating procedures should prescribe assessment and follow-up, which should include consideration of an investigation and/or corrective actions to avoid any further deterioration of the environment.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 — 環境監測計畫的雙重目的

環境監測 (Environmental Monitoring, EM) 計畫有兩個核心使命：

  • 持續性保證：確認潔淨室與潔淨空氣設備維持於設計與法規要求的潔淨度等級。
  • 偵測偏差：有效偵測環境超限事件，觸發調查與產品品質風險評估。

注意：EM 是「持續確認」（ongoing assurance），而非一次性驗證（one-time validation）。這是一個動態的品質系統工具。

核心概念解析 — 警戒限 vs 行動限

警戒限 (Alert Level)：為早期預警信號。超越此限值代表環境有惡化趨勢，需要評估並採取預防措施，但不一定需要立即停產。Alert level 應根據潔淨室驗證數據（qualification data）設定，並定期依趨勢資料複審。

行動限 (Action Limit)：為最高可接受上限，其最大值記載於 Table 5（非活性粒子）與 Table 6（活性微生物）。超越行動限必須啟動根本原因調查（root cause investigation）、評估產品衝擊，並實施矯正與預防措施（CAPA）。

關鍵差異：警戒限偏重趨勢管理；行動限偏重緊急回應。

比喻說明 — 醫院感染管控

想像一家醫院的感染管控計畫（Contamination Control Strategy, CCS）：警戒限就像「黃色警示」——病房出現幾例感冒患者，醫院要加強洗手與消毒頻率；行動限就像「紅色警示」——出現院內感染群聚事件，立即啟動隔離程序、停止非必要手術、調查感染源。

EM 計畫就是醫院的感染監控儀表板，讓管理者在問題惡化前早期介入。

重點提示 — 風險評估驅動的採樣設計

PIC/S Annex 1 明確要求：EM 計畫的採樣位置、頻率、方法與培養條件，必須來自風險評估（Risk Assessment），而非主觀決定。風險評估應涵蓋：

  • 製程與產品知識（process inputs, final product）
  • 廠房、設備的佈局與設計
  • 特定步驟的關鍵程度
  • 例行監測與驗證歷史數據
  • 環境中已知的典型微生物菌相（typical microbial flora）

稽查員常見問題：「你如何決定這個採樣點？」答案必須有文件化的風險評估支撐。

重點提示 — 趨勢分析的四大指標

9.11 條列四種需要關注的趨勢模式：

  • 超限次數增加：絕對值仍合格，但頻率上升。
  • 連續超越警戒限：表示系統性問題，非偶發。
  • 有共同原因的週期性超限：例如預防性維護後固定出現，代表維護作業本身需要改善。
  • 菌種變化：出現孢子形成菌（spore-forming microorganisms）或黴菌，尤其危險，因為這類微生物對一般消毒劑抵抗力強。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 假設 Grade B 區域連續三週的活菌計數均超越警戒限但未超越行動限，你的 SOP 應規定哪些後續動作？
  2. 一個採樣點在每次預防性維護後次日都出現行動限超標，這屬於哪種趨勢類型（9.11 條第幾項）？應如何根本解決？
  3. Grade A 區域出現黴菌（mould），應立即採取哪些步驟？是否影響已完成批次的放行決策？
9.14–9.21 非活性粒子監測 (Non-viable Particle Monitoring) 及 Table 5

原文內容 Original Text

9.14 A total particle monitoring program should be established to obtain data for assessing potential contamination risks and to ensure the maintenance of the environment for sterile operations in a qualified state.

9.15 The limits for environmental monitoring of airborne particle concentration for each graded area are given in Table 5.

Table 5: Maximum permitted total particle concentration for monitoring.

(a) For grade D, in operation limits are not predetermined. The manufacturer should establish in operation limits based on a risk assessment and on routine data, where applicable.

"Note 1: The particle limits given in the table for the 'at rest' state should be achieved after a short 'clean up' period defined during qualification (guidance value of less than 20 minutes) in an unmanned state, after the completion of operations (see paragraph 4.29)."
"Note 2: The occasional indication of macro particle counts, especially ≥ 5 µm, within grade A may be considered to be false counts due to electronic noise, stray light, coincidence loss etc. However, consecutive or regular counting of low levels may be indicative of a possible contamination event and should be investigated."

9.16 For grade A, particle monitoring should be undertaken for the full duration of critical processing, including equipment assembly.

9.17 The grade A area should be monitored continuously (for particles 0.5 and 5 µm) and with a suitable sample flow rate (at least 28 litres (1ft³) per minute) so that all interventions, transient events and any system deterioration is captured. The system should frequently correlate each individual sample result with alert levels and action limits at such a frequency that any potential excursion can be identified and responded to in a timely manner. Alarms should be triggered if alert levels are exceeded. Procedures should define the actions to be taken in response to alarms including the consideration of additional microbial monitoring.

9.18 It is recommended that a similar system be used for the grade B area although the sample frequency may be decreased. The grade B area should be monitored at such a frequency and with suitable sample size that the programme captures any increase in levels of contamination and system deterioration. If alert levels are exceeded, alarms should be triggered.

9.19 The selection of the monitoring system should take into account any risk presented by the materials used in the manufacturing operation (e.g. those involving live organisms, powdery products or radiopharmaceuticals) that may give rise to biological, chemical or radiation hazards.

9.20 In the case where contaminants are present due to the processes involved and would potentially damage the particle counter or present a hazard (e.g. live organisms, powdery products and radiation hazards), the frequency and strategy employed should be such as to assure the environmental classification both prior to and post exposure to the risk. An increase in viable particle monitoring should be considered to ensure comprehensive monitoring of the process. Additionally, monitoring should be performed during simulated operations. Such operations should be performed at appropriate intervals. The approach should be defined in the CCS.

9.21 The size of monitoring samples taken using automated systems will usually be a function of the sampling rate of the system used. It is not necessary for the sample volume to be the same as that used for formal classification of cleanrooms and clean air equipment. Monitoring sample volumes should be justified.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 — Table 5 解讀重點

Table 5 是無菌製造的「空氣品質護照」，每個等級在靜態（at rest）與動態（in operation）下的粒子限制都不同：

  • Grade A：靜態與動態完全相同（3,520 / 29），這是最嚴格的要求——即使有人員在場操作，粒子數也不能上升。這體現了 RABS 或隔離器的核心價值：將人員影響降至最低。
  • Grade B：靜態與 Grade A 相同，但動態下 0.5µm 粒子限制放寬至 352,000（約為靜態的 100 倍），反映人員存在的現實影響。
  • Grade C & D：限值逐步寬鬆，但 D 級動態限值「未預定（not predetermined）」，需廠商自行依風險評估設定。

公式與計算 — ISO 等級對應

Grade A = ISO 5 (靜態 + 動態)
Grade B = ISO 5 (靜態) / ISO 7 (動態)
Grade C = ISO 7 (靜態) / ISO 8 (動態)
Grade D = ISO 8 (靜態) / 未規定 (動態)

ISO 5 對應 ≥0.5µm: 3,520 /m³
ISO 7 對應 ≥0.5µm: 352,000 /m³
ISO 8 對應 ≥0.5µm: 3,520,000 /m³

Grade A 連續監測最低採樣流量：
  ≥ 28 L/min (= 1 ft³/min)

比喻說明 — 空氣品質監測站

Grade A 的連續粒子監測就像城市中的即時 PM2.5 監測站：每分鐘都在量測、每次超標都觸發警報，而不是每天早晨才看報告。這種即時性讓操作人員能在問題惡化前立即反應——例如在偶發干預後立即確認粒子數是否已恢復正常。

相比之下，Grade C/D 更像是定期採樣的氣象站，不需要每秒都更新。

重點提示 — Grade A 連續監測的技術要求

9.17 對 Grade A 的非活性粒子監測有三個硬性要求：

  • 連續監測（continuous）：涵蓋全部關鍵操作時程，包括設備組裝。
  • 最低流量：28 L/min（1 ft³/min）：確保樣本代表性，可捕捉短暫事件（transient events）。
  • 即時比對：每個採樣結果應即時與警戒限及行動限比對，超過警戒限需觸發警報，且程序需明確定義警報後的回應動作（包括是否追加活菌監測）。

注意：Grade B 亦建議類似系統，但可降低採樣頻率。

核心概念解析 — 特殊產品的監測策略（9.19-9.20）

某些產品類型可能損壞粒子計數器（particle counter）或造成危害：

  • 活菌製劑（live organisms）：如活菌疫苗、基因治療產品。
  • 粉末產品（powdery products）：乾粉吸入劑、凍乾粉末。
  • 放射性藥品（radiopharmaceuticals）。

策略：在風險暴露前後確認環境等級，增加活菌監測頻率，並在模擬操作中進行監測。所有策略需納入 CCS（污染控制策略）中。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 你的 Grade A 粒子計數儀的採樣流量是 20 L/min，符合 Annex 1 要求嗎？為什麼？
  2. Table 5 中 Grade B 靜態下 0.5µm 粒子限值與 Grade A 靜態相同，這背後的邏輯是什麼？
  3. Grade D 動態限值「未預定」——廠商應如何設定此限值？需要什麼類型的文件支撐？
9.22–9.31 活性微生物監測 (Viable Particle Monitoring) 及 Table 6

原文內容 Original Text

9.22 Where aseptic operations are performed, microbial monitoring should be frequent using a combination of methods such as settle plates (沉降碟), volumetric air sampling, glove, gown and surface sampling (e.g. swabs and contact plates). The method of sampling used should be justified within the CCS and should be demonstrated not to have a detrimental impact on grade A and B airflow patterns. Cleanroom and equipment surfaces should be monitored at the end of an operation.

9.23 Viable particle monitoring should also be performed within the cleanrooms when normal manufacturing operations are not occurring (e.g. post disinfection, prior to start of manufacturing, on completion of the batch and after a shutdown period), and in associated rooms that have not been used, in order to detect potential incidents of contamination which may affect the controls within the cleanrooms. In case of an incident, additional sample locations may be used as a verification of the effectiveness of a corrective action (e.g. cleaning and disinfection).

9.24 Continuous viable air monitoring in grade A (e.g. air sampling or settle plates) should be undertaken for the full duration of critical processing, including equipment (aseptic set-up) assembly and critical processing. A similar approach should be considered for grade B cleanrooms based on the risk of impact on the aseptic processing. The monitoring should be performed in such a way that all interventions, transient events and any system deterioration would be captured and any risk caused by interventions of the monitoring operations is avoided.

9.25 A risk assessment should evaluate the locations, type and frequency of personnel monitoring based on the activities performed and the proximity to critical zones. Monitoring should include sampling of personnel at periodic intervals during the process. Sampling of personnel should be performed in such a way that it will not compromise the process. Particular consideration should be given to monitoring personnel following involvement in critical interventions (at a minimum gloves, but may require monitoring of areas of gown as applicable to the process) and on each exit from the grade B cleanroom (gloves and gown). Where monitoring of gloves is performed after critical interventions, the outer gloves should be replaced prior to continuation of activity. Where monitoring of gowns is required after critical interventions, the gown should be replaced before further activity in the cleanroom.

9.26 Microbial monitoring of personnel in the grade A and grade B areas should be performed. Where operations are manual in nature (e.g. aseptic compounding or filling), the increased risk should lead to enhanced emphasis placed on microbial monitoring of gowns and justified within the CCS.

9.27 Where monitoring is routinely performed by manufacturing personnel, this should be subject to regular oversight by the quality unit (refer also to paragraph 8.19).

9.28 The adoption of suitable alternative monitoring systems such as rapid methods should be considered by manufacturers in order to expedite the detection of microbiological contamination issues and to reduce the risk to product. These rapid and automated microbial monitoring methods may be adopted after validation has demonstrated their equivalency or superiority to the established methods.

9.29 Sampling methods and equipment used should be fully understood and procedures should be in place for the correct operation and interpretation of results obtained. Supporting data for the recovery efficiency of the sampling methods chosen should be available.

9.30 Action limits for viable particle contamination are shown in Table 6.

Table 6: Maximum action limits for viable particle contamination

(a) Settle plates should be exposed in grade A and B areas for the duration of operations (including equipment set-up) and changed as required after a maximum of 4 hours (exposure time should be based on validation including recovery studies and it should not have any negative effect on the suitability of the media used).

For grade C and D areas, exposure time (with a maximum of 4 hours) and frequency should be based on QRM. Individual settle plates may be exposed for less than 4 hours.

(b) Contact plate limits apply to equipment, room and gown surfaces within the grade A and grade B areas. Routine gown monitoring is not normally required for grade C and D areas, depending on their function.

(c) It should be noted that for grade A, any growth should result in an investigation.

"Note 1: ...other methods can be used provided they meet the intent of providing information across the whole of the critical process where product may be contaminated (e.g. aseptic line set-up, aseptic processing, filling and lyophilizer loading)."
"Note 2: Limits are applied using CFU throughout the document. If different or new technologies are used that present results in a manner different from CFU, the manufacturer should scientifically justify the limits applied and where possible correlate them to CFU."

9.31 Microorganisms detected in the grade A and grade B areas should be identified to species level and the potential impact of such microorganisms on product quality (for each batch implicated) and overall state of control should be evaluated. Consideration should also be given to the identification of microorganisms detected in grade C and D areas (for example where action limits or alert levels are exceeded) or following the isolation of organisms that may indicate a loss of control, deterioration in cleanliness or that may be difficult to control such as spore-forming microorganisms and moulds and at a sufficient frequency to maintain a current understanding of the typical flora of these areas.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 — 活菌監測的四種方法

活性微生物監測（Viable Particle Monitoring）有四大主要採樣工具，各有適用場景：

  • 主動空氣採樣（Active Air Sampling）：使用衝擊式採樣器（impaction sampler）主動抽取已知體積的空氣，結果以 CFU/m³ 表示。優點：定量準確；缺點：設備本身可能干擾氣流。
  • 沉降碟（Settle Plate）：被動暴露的培養皿，讓空氣中微生物自然沉降。Grade A/B 需全程暴露（最長 4 小時）；結果反映暴露期間的整體污染情況。
  • 接觸碟（Contact Plate）：用來採集表面微生物，適用於設備、牆面、人員手套/無菌服。
  • 棉花棒採樣（Swab）：適用於不規則表面，如閥門、密封件。

實務上，Grade A/B 通常組合使用上述多種方法以確保全面覆蓋。

核心概念解析 — Table 6 解讀重點

Table 6 最關鍵的規定是 Grade A 任何微生物生長皆需調查（any growth → investigation）。這代表 Grade A 的微生物行動限實際上是「零容忍」（zero tolerance），與一般理解的數值限值不同。

其他重點：

  • Grade A/B 手套監測（glove print）分別為 <1 和 5 CFU/glove（含雙手共 10 根手指）。
  • Grade C/D 無手套監測要求（表示「—」）。
  • CFU = Colony Forming Unit（菌落形成單位）。若使用快速微生物方法（RMM），需科學驗證其與 CFU 的相關性。

比喻說明 — 沉降碟與主動採樣的互補性

主動空氣採樣就像「用吸塵器測量房間灰塵量」——主動、定量、即時。沉降碟則像「在桌上放一張白紙，過幾小時看有多少灰塵落下」——被動、但能反映整個操作期間的累積污染風險。

兩者各有優劣：主動採樣靈敏度高，但設備存在可能影響 Grade A 層流；沉降碟不干擾氣流，但受環境溫度、濕度影響培養基效能。故 Annex 1 要求兩者組合使用。

重點提示 — 人員監測的強化要求（9.25-9.26）

人員是無菌環境最大的污染源之一。Annex 1 要求：

  • 關鍵干預（critical intervention）後：至少監測外層手套，必要時監測無菌服相關部位。
  • 每次離開 Grade B 潔淨室時：監測手套與無菌服。
  • 手套監測後若超標：立即更換外層手套再繼續作業。
  • 無菌服超標：進行無菌服更換後方可繼續作業。

手動操作（manual aseptic compounding/filling）比自動化操作風險更高，CCS 中需特別強化人員無菌服監測的說明。

核心概念解析 — 快速微生物方法（Rapid Methods）

9.28 鼓勵廠商評估快速微生物監測方法（Rapid Microbial Methods, RMM），例如：

  • ATP 生物冷光法（ATP bioluminescence）
  • 流式細胞術（flow cytometry）
  • 自動化培養系統（automated incubation + imaging）

採用前提：必須經過驗證，證明其等效或優於傳統培養法。從監管角度，RMM 不能「偷工減料」——只有在科學上能證明不遜於傳統方法時，才可替代。

重點提示 — 菌種鑑定的要求（9.31）

Grade A/B 中偵測到的所有微生物必須鑑定到菌種層級（species level），並評估對已製造批次的潛在衝擊。這不只是技術要求，更是批次放行決策的重要依據。

實務影響：微生物實驗室需具備鑑定能力（如 MALDI-TOF 質譜儀或 16S rRNA 定序），或委外至合格實驗室。鑑定結果需納入 EM 調查報告中。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. Grade A 空氣採樣結果為 2 CFU/m³，根據 Table 6，這是否超過行動限？需要採取什麼行動？
  2. 沉降碟的最長暴露時間為 4 小時，但你的操作時間是 6 小時，應如何處理？
  3. 操作人員在一次關鍵干預後，其手套接觸碟結果為 3 CFU，Grade A 中，這是否需要調查？
9.32–9.36 無菌製程模擬 (APS) 設計與規劃

原文內容 Original Text

9.32 Periodic verification of the effectiveness of the controls in place for aseptic processing should include an APS using a sterile nutrient media and/or surrogate in place of the product. The APS should not be considered as the primary means to validate the aseptic process or aspects of the aseptic process. The effectiveness of the aseptic process should be determined through process design, adherence to the pharmaceutical quality system and process controls, training, and evaluation of monitoring data.

Selection of an appropriate nutrient media and/or surrogate should be made based on the ability of the media and/or surrogate to imitate physical product characteristics assessed to pose a risk to product sterility during the aseptic process. Where processing stages may indirectly impact the viability of any introduced microbial contamination, (e.g. aseptically produced semi-solids, powders, solid materials, microspheres, liposomes and other formulations where product is cooled or heated or lyophilized), alternative procedures that represent the operations as closely as possible should be developed. Where surrogate materials, such as buffers, are used in parts of the APS, the surrogate material should not inhibit the growth of any potential contamination.

9.33 The APS should imitate as closely as possible the routine aseptic manufacturing process and include all the critical manufacturing steps, specifically:

  1. The APS should assess all aseptic operations performed subsequent to the sterilisation and decontamination cycles of materials utilised in the process to the point where the container is sealed.
  2. For non-filterable formulations, any additional aseptic steps should be assessed.
  3. Where aseptic manufacturing is performed under an inert atmosphere, the inert gas should be substituted with air in the process simulation unless anaerobic simulation is intended.
  4. Processes requiring the addition of sterile powders should use an acceptable surrogate material in the same containers as those used in the process under evaluation.
  5. Separate simulations of individual unit operations (e.g. processes involving drying, blending, milling and subdivision of a sterile powder) should be avoided. Any use of individual simulations should be supported by a documented justification and ensure that the sum total of the individual simulations continues to fully cover the whole process.
  6. The process simulation procedure for lyophilized products should represent the entire aseptic processing chain including filling, transport, loading, a representative duration of the chamber dwell, unloading and sealing under specified, documented and justified conditions representing worst case operating parameters.
  7. The lyophilization process simulation should mimic all aspects of the process, except those that may affect the viability or recovery of contaminants. For instance, boiling-over or actual freezing of the solution should be avoided. Factors to consider include: the use of air to break vacuum instead of nitrogen or other process gases; replicating the maximum interval between sterilisation of the lyophilizer and its use; replicating the maximum period of time between filtration and lyophilization; and quantitative aspects of worst-case situations, e.g. loading the largest number of trays, replicating the longest duration of loading where the chamber is open to the environment.

9.34 The APS should take into account various aseptic manipulations and interventions known to occur during normal production as well as worst-case situations, and take into account the following:

  1. Inherent and corrective interventions representative of the routine process should be performed in a manner and frequency similar to that during the routine aseptic process.
  2. The inclusion and frequency of interventions in the APS should be based on assessed risks posed to product sterility.

9.35 APS should not be used to justify practices that pose unnecessary contamination risks.

9.36 In developing the APS plan, consideration should be given to the following:

  1. Identification of worst case conditions covering the relevant variables, such as container size and line speed, and their impact on the process.
  2. Determining the representative sizes of container/closure combinations to be used for validation. Bracketing or matrix approach may be considered for validation of the same container/closure configuration for different products where process equivalence is scientifically justified.
  3. Maximum permitted holding times for sterile product and equipment exposed during the aseptic process.
  4. The volume filled per container, which should be sufficient to ensure that the media contacts all equipment and component surfaces that may directly contaminate the sterile product. The volume used should provide sufficient headspace to support potential microbial growth and ensure that turbidity can be detected during inspection.
  5. The requirement for substitution of any inert gas used in the routine aseptic manufacturing process by air unless anaerobic simulation is intended.
  6. The selected nutrient media should be capable of growing a designated group of reference microorganisms as described by the relevant pharmacopeia and suitably representative local isolates.
  7. The method of detection of microbial contamination should be scientifically justified to ensure that contamination is reliably detected.
  8. The process simulation should be of sufficient duration to challenge the process, the operators that perform interventions, shift changes and the capability of the processing environment.
  9. Where the manufacturer operates different or extended shifts, the APS should be designed to capture factors specific to those shifts that are assessed to pose a risk to product sterility, for example the maximum duration for which an operator may be present in the cleanroom.
  10. Simulating normal aseptic manufacturing interruptions where the process is idle (e.g. shift changeovers, recharging dispensing vessels, introduction of additional equipment).
  11. Ensuring that environmental monitoring is conducted as required for routine production, and throughout the entire duration of the process simulation.
  12. Where campaign manufacturing occurs, such as in the use of Barrier Technologies or manufacture of sterile active substances, consideration should be given to designing and performing the process simulation so that it simulates the risks associated with both the beginning and the end of the campaign.
  13. The performance of "end of production or campaign APS" may be used as additional assurance or investigative purposes; however, their use should be justified in the CCS and should not replace routine APS.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 — APS 的定位與限制

無菌製程模擬（Aseptic Process Simulation, APS）又稱培養基灌充（Media Fill），是用無菌培養基（通常是 TSB，大豆酪蛋白胨液體培養基）代替真實藥品進行模擬充填，以驗證無菌操作的有效性。

重要認知：APS 不是無菌製程的「主要驗證手段」，而是定期確認（periodic verification）工具。無菌保證（sterility assurance）的根基是：製程設計 + 品質系統 + 製程管控 + 培訓 + 監測數據。APS 只是其中一環，但卻是最具說服力的整合性評估工具。

比喻說明 — APS 是「全系統壓力測試」

APS 就像銀行的災難恢復演練：平時一切看起來正常，但只有在模擬實際情境（包括各種突發狀況）下，才能真正確認應急流程是否有效。

培養基灌充中，「污染」等同於銀行演練中發現的漏洞——不是壞事，而是改進的機會。問題是：你的演練夠不夠真實、夠不夠嚴苛？

重點提示 — 培養基選擇的關鍵要求

培養基或替代物（surrogate）的選擇需考量：

  • 模擬真實產品特性：例如黏度、pH值，這些都可能影響潛在污染微生物的存活。
  • 不能抑制微生物生長：培養基灌充的目的是「讓污染顯現」，若培養基本身有抑菌性（如某些緩衝液），會掩蓋真實污染。
  • 特殊劑型：凍乾製劑、半固體、微球等需要特別設計替代程序，因為凍乾過程（升華、真空破空）可能影響微生物活力。
  • 凍乾模擬不能真正凍乾（避免培養基凍結或沸騰），但需模擬最長加載時間、腔室開放時間等最差情況。

核心概念解析 — 干預（Intervention）的模擬

APS 必須包含在常規生產中發生的所有類型干預：

  • 固有干預（Inherent Interventions）：製程本身不可避免的操作，如更換針頭、補充培養基。
  • 矯正干預（Corrective Interventions）：因設備故障、拒絕容器等需手動處理的操作。

重要原則：9.35 明確指出「APS 不應被用來合理化那些造成不必要污染風險的操作」——如果某種操作在 APS 中才特別謹慎，但日常生產卻不這麼做，那就違背了 APS 的精神。

公式與計算 — APS 設計的最差情況矩陣

APS 最差情況設計考量清單：

容器尺寸：最大 + 最小（bracketing approach）
充填速度：最慢線速（最長暴露時間）
操作人員數量：最多
班次更換：包含交班程序
製程中斷：換桶、加料、設備故障模擬
充填體積：足以覆蓋所有接觸面 + 留足培養空間
培養基濃度：符合 USP/EP/JP 要求
環境監測：與常規生產相同頻率

凍乾 APS 特殊要求：
  最長 lyophilizer 滅菌至使用間隔
  最長過濾至充填間隔
  最多托盤數 + 最長腔室開放時間

實務應用 Practical Application

在 CDMO 環境中，同一條充填線可能承接多個客戶的不同產品（如水針、凍乾、粉末針劑）。如何設計一套有效的 APS 計畫？

策略建議：

  • 使用 bracketing/matrix 方法，選擇代表性的容器規格，避免對每個規格都進行獨立 APS。
  • 針對凍乾產品，制定獨立的凍乾 APS 程序，涵蓋從充填到腔室開門的完整鏈條。
  • 確保每一條線路、每一個操作班次、每一位操作人員都涵蓋於 APS 計畫中。
  • 在每次改變線路配置（如更換容器規格）後，評估是否需要重新進行 APS。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 你的凍乾 APS 計畫中，是否需要真正執行凍乾程序？為什麼？應如何處理不能凍乾的限制？
  2. 在 APS 中，某位操作人員執行了一個在常規生產中不存在的干預動作，這樣的 APS 結果是否有效？
  3. 一條充填線有三個班次，APS 計畫應如何安排才能涵蓋所有班次的風險？
9.37–9.49 APS 執行、合格標準與失敗調查

原文內容 Original Text

9.37 For sterile active substances, batch size should be large enough to represent routine operation, simulate intervention operation at the worst case, and cover all surfaces that may come into contact with the sterile product. In addition, all the simulated materials (surrogates or growth medium) should be subjected to microbial evaluation. The simulation materials should be sufficient to satisfy the evaluation of the process being simulated and should not compromise the recovery of micro-organisms.

9.38 APS should be performed as part of the initial validation, with at least three consecutive satisfactory simulation tests that cover all working shifts that the aseptic process may occur in, and after any significant modification to operational practices, facilities, services or equipment which are assessed to have an impact on the sterility assurance of the product (e.g. modification to the HVAC system, equipment, changes to process, number of shifts and numbers of personnel, major facility shut down).

Normally, APS (periodic revalidation) should be repeated twice a year (approximately every six months) for each aseptic process, each filling line and each shift. Each operator should participate in at least one successful APS annually. Consideration should be given to performing an APS after the last batch prior to shut down, before long periods of inactivity or before decommissioning or relocation of a line.

9.39 Where manual operation (e.g. aseptic compounding or filling) occurs, each type of container, container closure and equipment train should be initially validated with each operator participating in at least 3 consecutive successful APS and revalidated with one APS approximately every 6 months for each operator. The APS batch size should mimic that used in the routine aseptic manufacturing process.

9.40 The number of units processed (filled) for APS should be sufficient to effectively simulate all activities that are representative of the aseptic manufacturing process. Justification for the number of units to be filled should be clearly captured in the CCS. Typically, a minimum of 5,000 to 10,000 units are filled. For small batches (e.g. those under 5,000 units), the number of containers for APS should at least equal the size of the production batch.

9.41 Filled APS units should be agitated, swirled or inverted before incubation to ensure contact of the media with all interior surfaces in the container. All integral units from the APS should be incubated and evaluated, including units with cosmetic defects or those which have gone through non-destructive in-process control checks. If units are discarded during the process simulation and not incubated, these should be comparable with units discarded during a routine fill, and only if production SOPs clearly specify that units must be removed under the same circumstances. In no case should more units be removed during a media fill intervention than would be cleared during a production run.

9.42 Where processes include materials that contact the product contact surfaces but are then discarded (e.g. product flushes), the discarded material should be simulated with nutrient media and be incubated as part of the APS, unless it can be clearly demonstrated that this waste process would not impact the sterility of the product.

9.43 Filled APS units should be incubated in a clear container to ensure visual detection of microbial growth. Where the product container is not clear (e.g. amber glass, opaque plastic), clear containers of identical configuration may be substituted to aid in the detection of contamination. When a clear container of identical configuration cannot be substituted, a suitable method for the detection of microbial growth should be developed and validated. Microorganisms isolated from contaminated units should be identified to the species level when practical, to assist in the determination of the likely source of the contaminant.

9.44 Filled APS units should be incubated without unnecessary delay to achieve the best possible recovery of potential contamination. The selection of the incubation conditions and duration should be scientifically justified and validated to provide an appropriate level of sensitivity of detection of microbial contamination.

9.45 On completion of incubation:

  1. Filled APS units should be inspected by personnel who have been appropriately trained and qualified for the detection of microbiological contamination.
  2. Samples of the filled units should undergo positive control by inoculation with a suitable range of reference organisms and suitably representative local isolates.

9.46 The target should be zero growth. Any contaminated unit should result in a failed APS and the following actions should be taken:

  1. an investigation to determine the most probable root cause(s);
  2. determination and implementation of appropriate corrective measures;
  3. a sufficient number of successful, consecutive repeat APS (normally a minimum of 3) should be conducted in order to demonstrate that the process has been returned to a state of control;
  4. a prompt review of all appropriate records relating to aseptic production since the last successful APS;
    • The outcome of the review should include a risk assessment of potential sterile breaches in batches manufactured since the last successful APS.
    • All other batches not released to the market should be included in the scope of the investigation. Any decision regarding their release status should consider the investigation outcome.
  5. all products that have been manufactured on a line subsequent to a process simulation failure should be quarantined until a successful resolution of the process simulation failure has occurred;
  6. where the root cause investigation indicates that the failure was related to operator activity, actions to limit the operator's activities, until retrained and requalified, should be taken;
  7. production should resume only after completion of successful revalidation.

9.47 All APS runs should be fully documented and include a reconciliation of units processed (e.g. units filled, incubated and not incubated). Justification for filled and non-incubated units should be included in the documentation. All interventions performed during the APS should be recorded, including the start and end time of each intervention and the involved person. All microbial monitoring data as well as other testing data should be recorded in the APS batch record.

9.48 An APS run should be aborted only under circumstances in which written procedures require commercial lots to be equally handled. An investigation should be documented in such cases.

9.49 An aseptic process should be subject to a repeat of the initial validation when:

  1. the specific aseptic process has not been in operation for an extended period of time; or
  2. there is a change to the process, equipment, procedures or environment that has the potential to affect the aseptic process or an addition of new product containers or container-closure combinations.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 — APS 頻率與人員資格

PIC/S Annex 1 對 APS 的頻率要求清晰且嚴格：

  • 初始驗證：至少 3 次連續合格，涵蓋所有工作班次。
  • 定期再驗證：每個製程、每條充填線、每個班次，每半年（約 6 個月）一次。
  • 操作人員：每人每年至少參與一次成功 APS（機器化操作）；手動操作需每人每 6 個月一次。
  • 手動操作初始驗證：每位操作人員需完成至少 3 次連續成功 APS。

APS 頻率與人員管理的連結，體現了「人員是最大污染風險」的核心認知。

公式與計算 — APS 充填數量規則

標準充填數量：
  最低 5,000 至 10,000 單位

小批次規則：
  批次 < 5,000 單位 → APS 數量 = 生產批次大小

合格標準：
  目標 = 零污染 (zero growth)
  任何污染 = 失敗 APS

失敗後再驗證要求：
  最少 3 次連續成功 APS 才可恢復生產

重要計算：
  APS 充填體積需足以：
  1. 接觸所有容器內表面
  2. 保留足夠頂空支持微生物生長
  3. 確保渾濁度於目視檢查中可見

重點提示 — APS 失敗的連鎖效應（9.46）

APS 失敗是製藥企業最嚴重的品質事件之一，其連鎖效應包括：

  • 立即停產：問題解決並完成再驗證前不得恢復生產。
  • 批次隔離：自上次成功 APS 以來，所有在該線生產的批次必須隔離（quarantine）。
  • 回溯調查：需回顧自上次成功 APS 以來的所有無菌生產記錄，進行無菌風險評估。
  • 未放行批次：需納入調查範圍，放行決策需基於調查結果。
  • 操作人員相關：若根本原因指向特定操作員，需限制該員活動，直到完成再培訓與再資格確認。

商業影響：一次 APS 失敗可能導致數週的停產損失，以及大量已充填批次的潛在廢棄——這是 APS 計畫設計嚴謹的最強動機。

比喻說明 — APS 失敗的「蝴蝶效應」

想像一間餐廳的健康稽查（衛生檢查）中被發現廚房有細菌污染。不只當天的食物要全部下架，所有自上次成功衛生稽查以來賣出的食物都需要溯源評估。餐廳必須關閉，直到通過連續三次衛生稽查。

APS 失敗的「蝴蝶效應」正是如此：問題不只影響這一批，而是所有「可能被污染的批次」都要接受審查。這正是為什麼 預防性的 APS 計畫設計遠比事後補救更重要。

核心概念解析 — 培育條件與陽性對照

APS 培育（incubation）有幾個關鍵點：

  • 不應有不必要的延遲：培育應在充填後盡快開始，以確保最佳微生物回收率。
  • 培育條件需驗證：溫度、時間需科學依據支持，確保對預期污染微生物的靈敏度。通常包括 20–25°C 和 30–35°C 兩段培育，以涵蓋不同類型微生物（黴菌/酵母菌 vs. 細菌）。
  • 陽性對照（Positive Control）：取部分充填單位接種已知參考菌株（包含本地環境分離菌株），確認培養基的促生長能力。若陽性對照無法生長，整批 APS 數據無效。
  • 透明容器：使用清晰的容器確保可目視偵測培育後的渾濁（turbidity）。琥珀瓶需使用相同結構的透明替代品，或發展其他偵測方法。

重點提示 — 不可培育單位的嚴格管控（9.41）

在 APS 中「不培育」的充填單位數量，必須與常規生產中同類情況廢棄的數量一致。不可藉由移除「可疑」單位來人為提高合格率。這是 FDA 和 EMA 稽查中常見的問題：

  • APS 中廢棄的單位不得多於常規生產中的廢棄數量。
  • 廢棄需有 SOP 明確依據（如干預後的固定數量清除）。
  • 與無菌組裝相關的廢棄單位通常單獨培育，不計入正式合格標準。

實務應用 — CDMO 業務場景

一個 CDMO 接受新客戶的委託充填，產品為 2mL 預充式注射器（PFS），計劃批次大小為 4,000 支。

根據 Annex 1 規定，初始 APS 計畫應如何設計？

  • 充填數量：小批次規則適用（<5,000 支）→ APS 充填數量應不少於 4,000 支。
  • 次數：至少 3 次連續成功 APS，涵蓋所有工作班次。
  • 操作人員：所有可能參與此產品充填的操作員均需參與。
  • 替代容器：若 PFS 筒身為透明玻璃，可直接使用；若有遮光塗層，需使用透明替代品或驗證其他偵測方法。
  • 培養基：選擇可模擬 2mL 水性注射液黏度特性的 TSB，並確認充填體積確保培養基接觸所有接觸面。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. APS 執行過程中，第 3,200 支因機器故障而停線 30 分鐘，重新啟動後繼續充填至 8,000 支。這次停線是否應記錄為干預？是否影響 APS 的有效性？
  2. 一批 APS（8,000 支）中發現 1 支污染，根本原因調查無法確定污染來源。此時應採取哪些步驟？自上次成功 APS（6 個月前）以來生產的批次如何處理？
  3. 某操作人員在 APS 中被鑑定為污染來源（手套計數超標且菌種與污染單位相同）。此操作人員需要經過哪些步驟才能重新參與無菌操作？

本節重點回顧 Section Summary

  • 環境監測計畫（9.4-9.13）：必須基於風險評估建立，涵蓋採樣位置、頻率、方法與培養條件；警戒限為早期預警，行動限為最高可接受限值；趨勢分析是 EM 計畫的核心，需定義並文件化趨勢監控程序。
  • 非活性粒子監測與 Table 5（9.14-9.21）：Grade A 需連續監測（≥28 L/min），超警戒限觸發警報；Grade A 靜態與動態粒子限值相同（3,520/m³, 29/m³）；Grade D 動態限值需廠商自行依風險評估設定。
  • 活性微生物監測與 Table 6（9.22-9.31）：Grade A 任何微生物生長均需調查（零容忍）；Grade A/B 的微生物需鑑定至菌種層級；人員監測（手套、無菌服）是重要且易被忽視的監測項目；快速微生物方法需驗證後方可採用。
  • APS 設計（9.32-9.36）：APS 是定期確認工具，非主要驗證手段；必須盡可能模擬常規製程的所有關鍵步驟與干預；凍乾製程需特別設計模擬程序；最差情況設計（worst case design）是 APS 的靈魂。
  • APS 執行與失敗（9.37-9.49）：目標為零污染（zero growth）；任何污染即為失敗 APS，需啟動完整調查流程、隔離相關批次、完成至少 3 次連續成功 APS 後才可恢復生產；每條線每個班次每半年一次；操作人員每人每年至少一次成功 APS。
  • 決策優先順序：無菌保證（Sterility Assurance）永遠是最高優先級，EM 計畫設計與 APS 的所有決策都必須以此為準則。
10

Section 10: Quality Control

品質管制 | p50-p52

Section 10: Quality Control (QC)

品質管控 — 無菌試驗、參數放行與快速微生物方法
PIC/S PE 009-16 Annex 1 (2022) — Manufacture of Sterile Medicinal Products | p50 - p52

本節學習目標

  • 理解無菌試驗 (Sterility Testing) 在無菌保證體系中的正確定位：它是最後一道防線，而非主要的保證工具
  • 掌握微生物負荷 (Bioburden) 測試的要求，包括無菌充填批次與終端滅菌批次的差異
  • 了解參數放行 (Parametric Release) 的前提條件與 bioburden 監控程序設計
  • 認識環境監測數據在批次放行審查中的角色，以及快速微生物方法 (Rapid Microbial Methods) 的應用情境
  • 掌握 QC 培養基的品質測試要求與 APS 媒介品質測試規定
10.1 – 10.2 人員與規格要求

原文內容 Original Text

10.1 There should be personnel available with appropriate training and experience in microbiology, sterility assurance and knowledge of the processes to support the design of the manufacturing activities, environmental monitoring regime and any investigation assessing the impact of microbiologically linked events to the safety of the sterile product.

10.2 Specifications for raw materials, components and products should include requirements for microbial, particulate and endotoxin/pyrogen limits when the need for this has been indicated by monitoring and/or by the CCS.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

QC 部門在無菌製造中的雙重角色：PIC/S Annex 1 Section 10 開門見山要求 QC 人員必須具備微生物學、無菌保證、製程知識三項核心能力。這不只是測試結果的接受與拒絕，而是參與設計（EM 制度設計）、調查（微生物事件根本原因分析）的主動角色。

污染控制策略 (CCS，Contamination Control Strategy) 是 Annex 1 2022 年版的核心新增概念。Section 2 定義 CCS，而 Section 10.2 強調：物料規格中是否需要設定微生物/顆粒/內毒素限度，必須由 CCS 驅動，而非由傳統習慣決定。

比喻說明 Analogy

想像醫院的感染控制小組：他們不只是在患者感染後才介入，而是主動設計隔離制度、訂定清潔頻率、審查環境數據——這正是 QC 微生物學家在無菌工廠中的角色。CCS 就是那份完整的「感染管控計畫 (Hospital Infection Control Plan)」，規格限度是其中明確的行動觸發點。

重點提示 Key Notes

10.2 的「when the need has been indicated by monitoring and/or CCS」是關鍵句——它意味著不是所有物料都需要設微生物限度，但一旦 CCS 評估認為有必要，就必須納入規格。這是 risk-based approach (基於風險的方法) 的體現，而非一刀切。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 你的 CDMO 工廠中，QC 微生物學家是否參與了 EM 制度的設計，或只是執行測試？兩者有何本質差異？
  2. 若一種輔料的供應商已提供微生物限度規格，你是否還需要在自己的規格中再定義？CCS 如何幫助你做這個決定？
10.3 – 10.4 Bioburden 測試要求

原文內容 Original Text

10.3 The bioburden assay should be performed on each batch for both aseptically filled product and terminally sterilised products and the results considered as part of the final batch review. There should be defined limits for bioburden immediately before the final sterilising grade filter or the terminal sterilisation process, which are related to the efficiency of the method to be used. Samples should be taken to be representative of the worst case scenario (e.g. at the end of hold time). Where overkill sterilisation parameters are set for terminally sterilised products, bioburden should be monitored at suitable scheduled intervals.

10.4 For products authorised for parametric release, a supporting pre-sterilisation bioburden monitoring programme for the filled product prior to initiating the sterilisation cycle should be developed and the bioburden assay should be performed for each batch. The sampling locations of filled units before sterilisation should be based on a worst case scenario and be representative of the batch. Any organisms found during bioburden testing should be identified and their impact on the effectiveness of the sterilising process determined. Where appropriate, the level of endotoxin/pyrogen should be monitored.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

微生物負荷 (Bioburden)：指在滅菌前，特定物品（如灌裝後的產品）上存在的微生物總量。Bioburden 不是汙染指標，而是一個關鍵的製程輸入參數：滅菌效率是以初始 bioburden 為基礎計算的。

為什麼每批都要做？ 10.3 要求 both 無菌充填與終端滅菌產品每批次都執行 bioburden。這與 overkill 製程的邏輯不同——overkill 可降低頻率（定期），但標準製程（non-overkill）必須每批監控。

參數放行 (Parametric Release)：以製程參數（溫度、時間、壓力等）替代無菌試驗作為放行依據。只有在製程已充分驗證、且每批 bioburden 受控的前提下才被允許。這是最高等級的製程理解與信任。

公式與概念 Bioburden 與 SAL 的關係

目標 SAL (Sterility Assurance Level) = 10⁻⁶

SAL = 初始 Bioburden × e^(-D × t/D-value)

更直觀地理解：
  若初始 bioburden = 1 CFU/unit
  → 需要 6-log reduction 達到 SAL 10⁻⁶

  若初始 bioburden = 100 CFU/unit
  → 需要 8-log reduction 達到 SAL 10⁻⁶

結論：bioburden 越高，達到相同 SAL 所需的
滅菌強度越大，或信心越低。

重點提示 Key Notes

取樣代表 worst case：10.3 強調樣品必須代表最壞情況，例如在 hold time 最末期取樣。這是因為微生物在等待時間內可能持續增殖，end-of-hold 是批次中 bioburden 最高的時間點。

Parametric release 的額外義務（10.4）：找到的菌株必須鑑定 (identified)，並評估其對滅菌效率的影響。耐熱菌（如芽孢桿菌）的存在，即使數量少，也可能危及 SAL 計算的有效性。

實務應用 Practical Application

CDMO 場景：客戶產品使用 121°C / 15 分鐘蒸汽滅菌（non-overkill）。你需要在 validation 階段建立 bioburden 限度（通常 ≤ 10 CFU/100 mL），並在每批灌裝後、啟動滅菌前取樣確認。如果某批 bioburden 超標，不能直接放行滅菌——必須調查原因並評估風險，可能需要拒批。這正是 bioburden data 進入批次放行決策的方式。

10.5 – 10.8 無菌試驗的正確定位

原文內容 Original Text

CRITICAL CONCEPTUAL POINT — Read Carefully

10.5 The sterility test applied to the finished product should only be regarded as the last in a series of critical control measures by which sterility is assured. It cannot be used to assure sterility of a product that does not meet its design, procedural or validation parameters. The test should be validated for the product concerned.

10.6 The sterility test should be performed under aseptic conditions. Samples taken for sterility testing should be representative of the whole of the batch but should in particular include samples taken from parts of the batch considered to be most at risk of contamination, for example:

  • i. For products which have been filled aseptically, samples should include containers filled at the beginning and end of the batch. Additional samples, e.g. taken after critical interventions should be considered based on risk.
  • ii. For products which have been heat sterilised in their final containers, samples taken should be representative of the worst case locations (e.g. the potentially coolest or slowest to heat part of each load).
  • iii. For products which have been lyophilized, samples taken from different lyophilization loads.
Note: Where the manufacturing process results in sub-batches (e.g. for terminally sterilised products) then sterility samples from each sub-batch should be taken and a sterility test for each sub-batch performed. Consideration should also be given to performing separate testing for other finished product tests.

10.7 For some products it may not be possible to obtain a sterility test result prior to release because the shelf life of the product is too short to allow completion of a sterility test. In these cases, the additional considerations of design of the process and additional monitoring and/or alternative test methods required to mitigate the identified risks should be assessed and documented.

10.8 Any process (e.g. Vaporized Hydrogen Peroxide, Ultra Violet) used to decontaminate the external surfaces of sterility samples prior to testing should not negatively impact the sensitivity of the test method or the reliability of the sample.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

重點提示 Key Notes — 最重要的概念轉變

無菌試驗 (Sterility Testing) 不能保證無菌！ 這是許多從業者最容易誤解的地方。10.5 的邏輯是：

  • 一批 10,000 支產品，隨機取 20 支做無菌試驗
  • 即使所有 20 支都通過，仍有 9,980 支未被測試
  • 統計學上，如果汙染率為 0.1%，這 20 支樣本仍有約 98% 機率全部通過

因此，無菌試驗是「確認型」的最後一步，而非「保障型」的主要防線。真正的無菌保證來自製程設計、驗證、與持續管控。

比喻說明 Analogy

無菌試驗就像餐廳最後上桌前試吃一口湯——它能告訴你這口鹹不鹹，但不能保證整鍋都沒問題。真正保障食品安全的是廚師的訓練、廚房的衛生環境、原料的新鮮度，以及標準化的烹調製程。試吃只是最後的確認，不是品質的來源。

核心概念解析 — 取樣策略

10.6 的取樣設計原則：樣品必須代表「最高風險時間點與位置」：

  • 無菌充填：批次開始（設備剛暴露）和結束（長時間暴露後）是風險最高點；關鍵干預後也應額外取樣。
  • 熱滅菌：滅菌釜中最冷點或加熱最慢的位置——這些點的 SAL 最低，代表批次的最壞情況。
  • 凍乾：不同凍乾批次的樣品，因為不同 load 的熱分佈可能不同。

短貨架期產品 (10.7) 的替代策略

標準無菌試驗：需時 14 天（薄膜過濾法）
問題：若產品 shelf life 僅 24-48 小時（如放射性藥物）
→ 無菌試驗完成前產品已過期！

替代方案（須文件化評估）：
  1. 強化製程驗證（更頻繁的 APS）
  2. 增加即時環境監測
  3. 快速微生物方法 (Rapid Microbial Methods)
     例如：螢光技術、ATP 生物發光法（2-4 小時出結果）
  4. 參數放行（若適用）

重點提示 — VHP 去汙不得損害試驗靈敏度 (10.8)

在樣品外表面使用 Vaporized Hydrogen Peroxide (VHP) 或紫外線去汙時，必須驗證這些處理不會滲入容器或殘留後影響培養基。如果去汙步驟殺死了真正存在的微生物，無菌試驗就成為「假陰性」的來源——這比沒有試驗更危險，因為給了虛假的安全感。

練習思考 Practice Questions

  1. 一個批次的無菌試驗失敗了（Sterility Test Failure, STF）。監管要求首先確認是「實驗室差錯」還是真正的批次問題。為什麼無菌試驗失敗不能直接等同於「這批產品不無菌」？反之，無菌試驗通過是否意味著「這批產品一定無菌」？
  2. 一個無菌充填批次，共灌裝 50,000 支，分成上午班和下午班各 25,000 支。取樣策略應如何設計才符合 10.6 的要求？
10.9 – 10.11 培養基品質測試與 EM 數據審查

原文內容 Original Text

10.9 Media used for product testing should be quality control tested according to the related Pharmacopeia before use. Media used for environmental monitoring and APS should be tested for growth promotion before use, using a scientifically justified and designated group of reference microorganisms and including suitably representative local isolates. Media quality control testing should normally be performed by the end user. Any reliance on outsourced testing or supplier testing of media should be justified and transportation and shipping conditions should be thoroughly considered in this case.

10.10 Environmental monitoring data and trend data generated for classified areas should be reviewed as part of product batch certification/release. A written procedure should be available that describes the actions to be taken when data from environmental monitoring are found out of trend or exceeding the established limits. For products with short shelf life, the environmental data for the time of manufacture may not be available; in these cases, the compliance should include a review of the most recent available data. Manufacturers of these products should consider the use of rapid/alternative methods.

10.11 Where rapid and automated microbial methods are used for general manufacturing purposes, these methods should be validated for the product(s) or processes concerned.

導師解析 Tutorial Commentary

核心概念解析 Key Concepts

Local isolates (在地分離菌株)：EM 培養基的 growth promotion testing 不只用藥典標準菌株，還必須納入你工廠實際環境中分離出的菌株。這是因為工廠特有的微生物可能對培養條件有特殊需求——若培養基對它們的生長不靈敏，EM 的假陰性率就會升高。

環境監測數據作為批次放行的一部分 (10.10)：這是 Annex 1 2022 年版的強化要求。EM 數據不只是環境管理的工具，而是批次放行決策的輸入。QP（Qualified Person，品質授權人）在簽署批次放行時，必須已審查相關的 EM 趨勢數據。

重點提示 Key Notes — Out of Trend (OOT) vs. Out of Specification (OOS)

OOT（超趨勢）：數據未超過行動限，但顯示上升趨勢——這是早期警告信號。Alert level 用於觸發 OOT 調查。OOS（超規格）：超過 Action limit，需要立即調查並採取糾正措施 (CAPA)。10.10 要求兩種情況都必須有書面程序規定後續行動。

快速方法 (Rapid Microbial Methods, RMM) 的驗證要求 (10.11)：方法必須針對你的具體產品或製程驗證，不能僅依賴廠商的通用驗證數據。驗證應包括：靈敏度、特異性、基質效應評估。

比喻說明 Analogy

培養基的 growth promotion testing 就像廚師在開餐前確認爐子能正常點火——如果爐子根本燒不起來，所有食材的「新鮮度測試」結果都毫無意義。Local isolates 的加入，就像用你家廚房常見的食材來測試，而不是用從沒見過的異國食材。

實務應用 Practical Application
